item_0.note: This case note concerns Greg Neltner in a multi-party motor vehicle accident matter, documented under the file label Greg-Neltner-MVA-4-1-2023. The work completed involved full file organization using an eight-bucket structure and content-based naming. Phase 1 established a complete inventory and setup for parallel processing.

In Phase 1, the team generated a file inventory totaling 253 files. They scrambled 177 .md filenames to eliminate naming bias, created a PDF-to-MD mapping for reunification, and split the inventory into 16 chunks to enable parallel processing. Phase 2 followed with a parallel workflow involving 16 sub-agents, each analyzing roughly 11 files. The analysis was based solely on file content, with no reliance on filenames, and a comprehensive reorganization map was created for all 253 files. The team applied a standardized naming convention: YYYY-MM-DD - Client Name - Category - Originator - Description. They identified 15 duplicate court filing emails for deletion and noted that the case involved multiple parties, with Cecelia Neltner-specific documents found within Greg’s folder.

Phase 3, the Quality Review, completed with an error rate of 1.5% (3 errors out of about 200 files checked). The main agent corrected three issues: two files were incorrectly marked as duplicates when they were, in fact, different court filings from different dates (8/26/2024 and 2/12/2025), and one file was mis-categorized as "Negotiation Settlement" when it should have been "Litigation" (a deposition scheduling email). Additionally, the team verified that the 15 duplicate court filing emails were safe to delete.

Phase 4, Execution, involved 252 file operations. A total of 243 files were moved into the proper eight-bucket structure with the following distribution: Litigation 113 files (covering discovery, depositions, court filings, and notices); Client 45 files (communications, intake, voicemails); Medical Records 19 files (seven providers with subdirectories); Insurance 16 files (BI/Progressive, PIP/State Farm, PIP/KY Assigned Claims); Investigation 12 files (police reports, property damage photos); Expenses 10 files (court reporter invoices); Negotiation Settlement 7 files (demand letters); Case Information 16 files (JSON data files); and Lien 1 file (State Farm subrogation). The team deleted 15 duplicate court filing notification emails, and no PDF reunification was required because there were no PDFs in this case—the documents were already in .md, .eml, .docx, or .jpg formats.

Phase 5, Verification, confirmed that all eight bucket directories were properly organized, and naming convention compliance was 100%. Companion file matching was also 100% (all EML files had corresponding .md companions). Ten files remained in the root directory (about 4%): two were flagged for poor OCR quality, four were deposition transcript duplicates (PTX/TXT versions), two were case data files, and two were uncategorized court emails. In total, 243 of 253 files were organized, representing 96% completion.

Critical case information uncovered includes: a multi-party matter with Greg Neltner and Cecelia Neltner as co-plaintiffs against Trinity Cohara; active litigation in Boone Circuit Court (Case 24-CI-00452); depositions completed for Greg Neltner and Cecelia Neltner on 9/17/2024; Trinity Cohara’s deposition scheduled for 3/21/2025 at 2:00 PM; defense counsel listed as Richardson Law Group (Katie Nelson, Josh Leckrone, Maeve Weihl); Progressive (BI carrier) denied liability on [DOB-1]; State Farm PIP paid $6,000 to Southgate Chiropractic (claim #1747Q474T); State Farm subrogation lien of $6,000 (letter dated 10/9/2024); settlement demands sent by Greg on 10/3/2023 and by Cecelia on [DOB-2]; a medical update noting Greg went to the ER on 2/13/2025 for chronic arthritis of the C3 region and other areas; medical providers involved include Southgate Chiropractic (primary), St Elizabeth Healthcare, St Elizabeth Primary Care, BUC Independence LLC (Cecelia), and New Orleans Orthopedic Institute.

Result: The case file is now organized within a proper eight-bucket structure using a standardized naming convention, with files correctly categorized and easily retrievable. Quality metrics indicate 98.5% initial accuracy, 100% accuracy after main agent corrections, and 100% duplicate detection accuracy following those corrections.

item_17.note: In the Neltner v. Cohara matter, the case is recorded as Greg-Neltner-MVA-4-1-2023, with Greg Neltner as the client. The note you provided is a sequence of email communications among counsel discussing scheduling for mediation and a Zoom deposition related to the matter. The email thread begins with W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, writing to Katie Nelson Dunn and Whitney Moore of Richardson Law Group, with cc’d Filevine project email addresses for Greg Neltner and Cecelia Neltner (MVA 4/1/2023). The July 7, 2025 email from Bryce asks Katie for the Zoom link for “tomorrow’s mediation,” and Bryce’s firm contact details are provided: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-554]; fax [PHONE-553]. The message includes the standard privilege and error-notice disclaimer typical of these firm emails.

The email chain contains several messages from May 15, 2025 that revolve around scheduling dates. In one message, Bryce writes: “Not a worry - the 8th at 1pm it is.” This appears to be a confirmation of a date and time, presumably for the mediation. In a companion message, Whitney Moore indicates that Linda’s office advised the 8th is available to them, though there had been a misunderstanding because another assistant had requested the date and it had appeared as taken. Whitney adds: “If you are still good for the 8th at 1pm zoom we will have it confirmed.” Whitney’s message includes her Richardson Law Group signature block, which lists 334 Beechwood Road Suite 502, Ft. Mitchell, KY 41017; phone [PHONE-552]; fax [PHONE-551], and her email address [EMAIL-550], along with links to the firm’s website and the usual environment notice.

Earlier in the thread, Bryce indicates: “July 9 will work for me.” In response, Katie (from Richardson Law Group) explains that Linda’s office informed them Linda is no longer available on July 8 and asks whether Bryce is available for a Zoom deposition on July 9, July 10, or July 17. Bryce replies with the remark “No Zoom would be great,” followed by his signature. He later reiterates, “July 9 will work for me,” in another message, and Katie again references Linda’s unavailability on July 8 and asks about the July 9, 10, or 17 options for the Zoom deposition. After this, Bryce confirms that “July 9 will work for me” and indicates the possibility of a Zoom depo on those dates. The thread includes the usual attorney-client privilege notices and the firm contact details for both The Whaley Law Firm and Richardson Law Group.

The May 15 sequence also contains the standard notices present in each email, including disclaimers about privilege, instructions to contact the sending firm if the message was received in error, and reminders about not forwarding the content to unauthorized recipients. The May messages also show the email signatures with the respective firm details and contact information, and in Whitney Moore’s message there are embedded images (cid:image001.png, cid:image002.png, cid:image003.png) within the email body, as well as a notice encouraging environmental consideration before printing.

In summary, the thread documents ongoing scheduling discussions in May 2025 for a Zoom deposition and a mediation in the Neltner v. Cohara matter, with Greg Neltner’s counsel seeking to coordinate dates and obtain the Zoom link for the mediation set around early July. The parties alternately considered July 8 at 1:00 PM (which Linda’s office later indicated was no longer available), and July 9 (with July 10 or July 17 as alternatives for the Zoom deposition), while Bryce and Katie and Whitney continued to negotiate preferred dates. The July 7, 2025 email from Bryce to Katie about obtaining the Zoom link for “tomorrow’s mediation” closes the note, with the cc’d Filevine addresses for Greg and Cecelia Neltner and the same firm contact details and privilege notices appearing in the thread.

item_20.note: The case at hand is Greg-Neltner-MVA-4-1-2023, concerning Greg Neltner in the matter Neltner v. Cohara. The notes summarize a sequence of email exchanges between counsel at The Whaley Law Firm and Richardson Law Group regarding scheduling for a deposition/mediation in the Neltner v. Cohara matter. The thread begins with a May 6, 2025 exchange and continues through May 15, 2025, with multiple proposed dates in July 2025 and differing preferences about whether the proceedings should be conducted by Zoom.

In the May 6, 2025 correspondence, Katie Nelson Dunn of Richardson Law Group (the recipient in the chain) sent Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm a list of available dates and noted that the second week of July onward was fairly open; she asked Bryce to indicate which date would work and that she would confirm with their claims professional. Bryce replied that the afternoon of Tuesday, July 8 would be great. He signed the message as W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm, and included his office address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, along with his phone and fax numbers. The email chain includes the standard attorney‑client privilege disclaimer and confidentiality notices, as well as an invitation to consider the environment before printing.

On May 15, 2025, further scheduling discussions occurred. Katie informed Bryce that Linda Hopgood’s office had advised that Linda would no longer be available on July 8, and she asked whether Bryce could do July 9, 10, or 17 for a Zoom deposition. In a reply from Bryce, he stated, “No Zoom would be great,” indicating a preference for proceeding without a Zoom format. The thread also contains the typical external-email warnings and confidentiality notices that accompany the correspondence, including the reminder that the message is intended only for the named recipients and should not be forwarded to unauthorized individuals.

Later on May 15, 2025, Katie responded with an alternative: Linda Hopgood was available on July 8 at 1 PM via Zoom, and she asked whether there were any objections to conducting the mediation by Zoom. item_39.note: This note concerns Case: Greg-Neltner-MVA-4-1-2023, involving client Greg Neltner and Progressive Claim #23-6275504. The communication chain centers on negotiations following a motor vehicle accident in which Greg Neltner and Cecilia Neltner are the clients, and the opposing party is Ms. Cohara.

On February 27, 2025 at 02:07:24 PM (GMT-05:00), Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to Megan Renfro of Progressive, with copies to two Filevine project email addresses. In the message, Bryce stated that, as discussed with Ms. Nelson, they were unable to negotiate the claim on the basis of split liability. His clients have testified consistently that Ms. Cohara bears responsibility for the collision. He noted that Ms. Cohara did not appear to testify at her previously scheduled deposition, and that the deposition has been rescheduled to 03/21/25. Bryce signed as *W. Bryce Koon, Esq.* of The Whaley Law Firm, with full contact details, and the message included The Whaley Law Firm’s address and phone/fax numbers. The electronic message also contained a standard attorney-client privilege/confidentiality notice instructing that it is intended only for the named recipient, and specifying that disclosure or forwarding is prohibited if received in error.

Earlier that same day, February 27, 2025 at approximately 2:03 PM, Megan E. Renfro replied to Bryce. She asked whether he had spoken with his clients, Gregory and Cecilia Neltner, and whether they had any responses to Progressive’s offers.

This exchange followed a series of prior communications. On January 21, 2025 at 3:08 PM, Megan Renfro sent Bryce a message confirming offers discussed during a conversation about the Neltner clients. The message stated: “Bryce, Thank you for speaking with me today regarding clients Gregory and Cecilia Neltner. Please allow this to confirm my offers of $1,500 for Gregory and $500 for Cecilia. Both offer are inclusive of any and all liens, exclusive of PIP and inclusive of your firm obtaining a dismissal. Please review these offers with your clients. I look forward to working with you.” The message was signed by Megan Renfro, Sr. Claims Specialist, The Progressive Group of Insurance Companies, and included Progressive’s mailing address, office hours, and contact information, along with a confidentiality disclaimer and a note to track the claim online.

On February 7, 2025 at 7:25 AM, Megan Renfro again emailed Bryce, following up to see if he had a chance to speak with his clients and whether they had a response to the offers. The message reiterated the same contact details and confidentiality language found in the later exchanges.

In summary, the record shows Progressive’s initial offers of $1,500 for Gregory Neltner and $500 for Cecilia Neltner (inclusive of all liens, exclusive of PIP, and including the firm obtaining a dismissal), with repeated requests for the Neltners to review and respond. Progressive sought confirmation of any response from the Neltner clients after Bryce’s discussions, while Bryce’s February 27 email documented that the defense maintains that Ms. Cohara bears responsibility for the collision and noted the rescheduling of Ms. Cohara’s deposition to 03/21/25 due to her failure to appear at the prior deposition.

item_46.last_activity: 2025-02-12T00:00:00
item_46.note: Case: Greg-Neltner-MVA-4-1-2023. Client: Greg Neltner. Re: Neltner v. Cohara.

In the Neltner v. Cohara matter, dated communications circulated in February 2025 regarding taking the deposition of Mrs. Cohara. On February 12, 2025, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager for The Whaley Law Firm, emailed Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm, with Katie Nelson of Richardson Law Group and others copied, to transmit an Amended Notice to Take the Deposition of Mrs. Cohara for March 21, 2025, beginning at 2:00 p.m. at the recipient’s office. Tuttle invited any questions or requests for further discussion and provided her contact information: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; direct line [PHONE-482]; office line [PHONE-481] ext. 104; email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (noting a new email address). The message also contained the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer.

The scheduling conversation began earlier in the year. On January 31, 2025, Bryce Koon replied to Katie Nelson with a plan to be out of town on that date and asked whether there were other possible dates in March that might work. In Katie Nelson’s prior message, dated January 31, 2025 at 12:47 p.m., she had proposed that Ms. Cohara be deposed on March 7, any time after 1:00 p.m., and she suggested holding the deposition at their Ft. Mitchell office, as had been done for the Plaintiffs, asking to know if this date would work.

In a sequence of exchanges on February 12, 2025, the topic focused on March 21 or other dates. Katie asked whether March 14 or 21 could work. Sarena replied that Bryce was available on March 21, 2025 and that their office would be suitable, but they requested an 11:30 a.m. start time to allow travel to Ft. Mitchell. Katie responded that her client was only available in the afternoon and asked whether a 1:30 p.m. or 2:00 p.m. start time would work for Bryce. Sarena said she would double-check with Bryce and get back to Katie as soon as possible. The exchange included standard email notices and multiple copies to the involved attorneys, with the following participants and roles: Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm; W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm; Katie Nelson, Associate at Richardson Law Group, PLLC; and Josh Leckrone of Richardson Law Group, among others CC’d on the correspondence.

In summary, after initial scheduling discussions for March 7, and then proposed alternatives of March 14 or March 21, the team settled on March 21, 2025, with a preferred 11:30 a.m. start initially noted by the Whaley team to allow travel time. However, after considerations of the afternoon availability of the deponent, the parties ultimately confirmed a deposition on March 21, 2025, beginning at 2:00 p.m., to be held at the recipient’s office, via the Amended Notice attached by Sarena Tuttle.

item_121.note: On August 23, 2024, at 4:31 PM Eastern, the Boone Circuit Court filed a Notice of Electronic Filing in the matter captioned NELTNER, Greg et al. v. COHARA, Trinity ( Boone County Circuit Court, Case 24-CI-00452). The case, identified as envelope 8669369, involves Greg Neltner and others as plaintiffs against Trinity Cohara. The notice was generated by the Kentucky Court of Justice eFiling system and originated from [EMAIL-277].

The eFiling was filed by Kathleen Nelson, attorney for the defendant, and the notice was electronically mailed to the following recipients: Aaron Gregory Whaley ([EMAIL-278]), Joshua J. Leckrone ([EMAIL-279]), and Kathleen Nelson ([EMAIL-315]). The notice indicates that two documents were included in this eFiling: two copies of “NOTICE TO TAKE DEPOSITION.” A link is provided to view the documents at https://kcoj.kycourts.net/eFilingRetrieval/Home/Package?id=534C580E-150F-4567-9335-A260C6F07B5E.

This message was automatically generated by the Kentucky Court of Justice eFiling system and is not to be replied to. Mitchell office. The proposed structure was to start with Greg at 10:00 AM, Cecilia at noon, and to consider a potential 2:00–3:00 PM start for the defendant’s deposition if needed. item_169.note: Case: Greg-Neltner-MVA-4-1-2023. Client: Greg Neltner. This note concerns the written discovery requests from the defense attorney related to Greg Neltner’s motor vehicle accident case. The communication thread began with an email sent on Friday, July 12, 2024, at 2:34:17 PM Eastern Time from Sarena Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, to Cecelia Neltner and Greg Neltner, with Bryce Koon CC’d. The subject of the message was Re: Your Written Discovery Requests from the Defense Attorney.

In the body of the email to Cecelia, Sarena stated that they were needing copies of Cecelia’s driver’s license and/or state ID, a copy of Cecelia’s health insurance cards, and Cecelia’s records from Children’s Hospital. Sarena noted that every time they had attempted to obtain Cecelia’s records from Children’s Hospital, the hospital indicated that their authorization to obtain those records had been revoked by Cecelia. Sarena also advised that she would be sending documents for Cecelia to sign via DocuSign and instructed Cecelia to follow the prompts to execute the documents from any electronic device without printing them.

In the same thread, Sarena addressed Greg, informing him that they were also needing a few things from him. She said that they had sent Greg some documents via DocuSign for his execution but had not yet received them back. She reiterated the need for a copy of Greg’s driver’s license and/or state ID and his health insurance cards. Sarena additionally requested that Greg provide the name of his Primary Care Provider (PCP) and the names of any other doctors he had seen in the past twenty years or so. She closed by inviting either party to contact The Whaley Law Firm directly at [PHONE-397], ext. 104, or ext. 114 with any questions. The signature block followed, identifying Sarena M. Tuttle as Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222), direct line (D: [PHONE-398]), office line (O: [PHONE-399] ext 104), and email (E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com), along with a note to please use the new email address.

Later that day, on Friday, July 12, 2024, at 2:01 PM (time indicated with an uncertain formatting), Cecelia Neltner replied. She wrote that she had a lot going on and had lost track of what she still needed to do. She asked if it was possible for The Whaley Law Firm to send her the documents and/or a list of tasks she needed to complete, noting that her email was heavily backed up and she could not locate all of the firm’s emails. She expressed that receiving those items would be very helpful.

The thread also contains earlier correspondence from June 2024. On Tuesday, June 11, 2024, at 10:24 AM, Sarena Tuttle wrote to Cecelia. She thanked Cecelia and then explained that it appeared Cecelia had answered her father’s set of questions. Sarena directed Cecelia to review the initial email and to provide her own answers to the set propounded to Cecelia, emphasizing that the cover letter and the emboldened title would bear Cecelia’s name, not her father’s.

The chain shows an earlier exchange on Monday, June 10, 2024. At 11:44 AM, Sarena Tuttle sent Greg and Cecelia a message explaining that the attached Discovery Requests from the Defense Attorney in their claim had been provided. The message noted that there was a packet for each of them, and while the questions would be almost identical, each person should provide their own independent responses. Sarena requested that both Greg and Cecelia supply a complete list of the providers each had seen for treatment, including their PCP, and asked them to include a personal description of the accident from their own viewpoint. She welcomed questions and offered to discuss them further.

The thread also indicates that Cecelia had sent a message on Monday, June 10, 2024, at 7:09 PM, though the contents of that message are not shown in the record excerpt provided.

The contact information for Sarena M. Tuttle, as listed in the signature blocks, includes her role as Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, the firm’s address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222), the direct line (D: [PHONE-400]), the office line (O: [PHONE-401] ext 104), and the email address Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, with a note indicating a new email address. The Whaley Law Firm’s general contact details, including the phone number for general inquiries and the extension numbers referenced above, are consistently referenced across the messages.

item_226.last_activity: 2023-12-12T00:00:00
item_226.note: Case: Greg-Neltner-MVA-4-1-2023 involve Greg Neltner and Progressive Insurance in a motor-vehicle accident matter identified as PROGRESSIVE 23-6275504. The core dispute centers on fault for a rear-end collision in which Progressive’s insured apparently crossed lanes to pull in front of Greg Neltner. Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm represents Greg Neltner, and Amy Morris is the Progressive claims specialist handling the file. The exchange spans multiple emails between October 2023 and December 2023, with a focus on conflicting accounts of how the incident occurred and what the police report shows.

The discussion began with an October 17, 2023 email from Amy Morris to Aaron Whaley and Justin Whaley, attaching Progressive’s formal response to the demand for Gregory Neltner. The thread then shows a sequence of later messages in which the parties dispute what happened and what the police report reflects. By late November and early December 2023, the disagreements had become more concrete: Progressive’s insured says she had been sitting at a red light waiting to turn for a couple of minutes, while the police report indicates that she cut across three lanes of traffic to turn left and, in doing so, turned suddenly in front of Greg Neltner. The parties acknowledge the collision as a rear-end event, but the implication is that the insured’s lane-changing maneuver is what caused the incident, a point contested by Greg Neltner’s side.

On November 30, 2023, Aaron Whaley asked Amy Morris to share photos, specifically inquiring whether the photos were taken at the scene. He stated that the evidence before them included statements from Greg and Cecelia Neltner and the insured’s statement, and acknowledged that everyone agrees it was a rear-end collision. He emphasized that the critical question was whether the insured drove across three lanes to pull in front of Greg Neltner, noting that the only evidence of that maneuver would be the insured’s statement to the police officer who prepared the scene narrative. He also pointed out that the officer could testify to what the insured said, since the officer relied on those statements in making a liability decision, and that Greg Neltner’s recorded statement indicated he did not see the insured. He highlighted that the accident report described the insured as having “suddenly turned in front of him, leaving him no time to react,” and he noted that the insured’s vehicle damage was listed as 7 o’clock, supposedly consistent with the cross-lane left-turn scenario.

Amy Morris responded on December 6, 2023, stating that the police report contained several discrepancies concerning the time and location of the loss. She summarized Progressive’s insured as claiming to be sitting still at a red light when rear-ended and pointed to Progressive’s damage photos supporting a direct rear-end impact. Based on the information available, Progressive maintained a liability denial and invited any evidence that could support the other side’s position for review.

On December 6, 2023, later that afternoon, Aaron Whaley replied, requesting copies of photos and clarifying that there was no body-camera footage available. He reiterated the evidentiary posture: Greg and Cecelia Neltner’s statements on one hand, Progressive’s insured’s statement on the other, with a consensus that the collision was a rear-end event. He emphasized that the crucial issue was whether the insured crossed three lanes to pull in front of Greg Neltner, noting that the only evidence for that maneuver was the insured’s statement to the responding officer. He described the officer’s liability decision as based on what the insured said and pointed out that Greg Neltner’s recorded statement stated he did not see the insured, which aligned with the police report’s account that the insured “suddenly turned in front of him, leaving him no time to react.” He also mentioned that the insured’s vehicle damage being listed at 7 o’clock would be consistent with her account of crossing three lanes to the left.

On December 12, 2023, Amy Morris replied that she had been out of the office on Thursday and Friday but would share the requested information if the other party would share photos of their client’s damage. She explained that Progressive’s insured’s statement differed from what was in the police report and that the other party’s client had not seen Progressive’s insured. She acknowledged a discrepancy in the reported time and location and described the police report’s sequence as Burlington Pike, then KY 18, then the off-ramp. She noted that maps suggested Burlington Pike is KY 18 and that the loss occurred at the light where the insured was waiting to get onto the ramp, calling that portion a confusing part of the narrative.

That same day, December 12, 2023, at 1:32 p.m. (approximately), Amy’s message conveyed her continuing concern about the discrepancies between the insured’s statement and the police report, including the location and timing issues, and she reiterated Progressive’s liability position for review upon receipt of additional information to compare against the insured’s account and any photos.

Finally, later on December 12, 2023, Aaron Whaley responded that the central dispute remained the insured’s claim that she had waited at the light for a couple of minutes, versus the police report’s description of her crossing three lanes to turn left and pulling in front of Greg Neltner. He stated that, in the absence of other corroboration, it would be a matter of the plaintiff’s word against your insured’s word, but if the insured’s claim that she had waited at the light for a couple of minutes were true, he would call the police officer to testify to what the insured told him at the scene. He noted that the police report’s narrative appeared to have come from both parties and that the ultimate question would be whether the jury believed Progressive’s insured over Greg Neltner and the police officer—a difficult position to be in at trial.

In summary, the record reflects an ongoing, back-and-forth exchange over fault in a rear-end collision between Greg Neltner and Progressive’s insured, with key evidentiary points centering on discrepancies between the insured’s account (waiting at a red light to turn, no lane-crossing), the police report’s account (the insured crossing three lanes to pull in front of Greg), the jurisdictional location sequence (Burlington Pike, KY 18, NB 75 ramp), and the availability of photos or body-camera footage to corroborate the narratives. The file also shows that Progressive’s counsel sought to rely on the police officer’s testimony about statements made at the scene and on the police report’s portrayal of the insured’s statements, while Greg Neltner’s side emphasized the consistency of their statements and the potential weight of the officer’s testimony, with the liability decision likely resting with how a jury would assess credibility.

item_231.note: Case: Greg-Neltner-MVA-4-1-2023. Client: Greg Neltner. The matter centers on correspondence related to Progressive file 23-6275504 and involves attorney Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm and Progressive Claims Specialist Amy Morris, with Greg and Cecelia Neltner as the affected party.

On December 6, 2023, at 4:19 PM (Eastern Time), Aaron Whaley sent an external email to Amy Morris requesting that Progressive share the photos from the scene. Whaley stated that he had Greg and Cecelia Neltner’s statements and that Progressive had its own insurance statement. He noted that all parties agree the incident was a rear-end collision, and that the sole dispute concerns whether Progressive’s insured drove across three lanes of traffic to pull in front of his client; Whaley asserted that the insured’s police statement admitting the lane-crossing is strong and admissible evidence. He asked how the time and location of the loss could be wrong and commented that, in the end, it would be his client’s word and the police officer’s word against the insured’s.

Amy Morris replied later that day, explaining that there are discrepancies in the police report regarding the time and location of the loss. She stated that their insured claimed they were sitting still at a red light when rear-ended, and that Progressive’s damage photos support a direct rear-end collision. Based on the information available, she said Progressive was standing by its liability denial and requested any evidence from Whaley to review in support of the other stance.

Earlier communications in the thread show Whaley’s prior exchanges. On November 30, 2023, at 4:15 PM, Whaley thanked Morris for the update and referenced an attached response to an open records request. He indicated that there was no body camera footage and emphasized that the police report was the crucial document, detailing what the insured said to the officer at the scene and aligning with both the insured’s statement and Greg Neltner’s account. He noted that the police report stated Progressive’s insured “crossed three lanes of traffic to get onto the NB 75 ramp, and as she did so, she turned in front of” Whaley’s client. While the officer could not testify to what occurred since he did not witness it, he could testify to what the insured said. He pointed out that the officer based his liability decision on the insured’s statements. The recorded statement from Greg Neltner indicated he did not see the insured, and the accident report described the insured as having “suddenly turned in front of him, leaving him no time to react.” The damage to the insured’s vehicle was listed as 7 o’clock, which Whaley argued was consistent with the insured’s statement about crossing three lanes to the left.

In another exchange from November 30, 2023, at 3:58 PM, Amy Morris reiterated that this was a word-vs-word case. The insured claimed they were rear-ended, while the client stated he did not know what happened and did not see the other vehicle. Morris referenced a third version in the police report and reiterated a desire to review bodycam footage, maintaining that Progressive was advocating for its insured given the information available at that time.

Earlier emails in the thread include Amy Morris’s messages to Whaley from November 29, 2023, at 2:05 PM, in which she stated she had received a voicemail and that Progressive remained by its liability decision, awaiting bodycam footage for review. A prior message from November 9, 2023, at 12:24 PM noted that the reply was sent to Aaron Whaley on October 17, 2023, and acknowledged ongoing discussion about the file. On October 17, 2023, Morris attached a formal response to the demand for Gregory Neltner. And on June 28, 2023, Morris asked Whaley to provide an email address for Jessa, also including her contact information and signature.

The case file also contains standard contact details for the parties: Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm, located at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, phone number [PHONE-498]; Amy Morris of Progressive Insurance Companies, with address at 9520 Ormsby Station Road, Suite 200, Louisville, KY 40223, and direct lines and email as noted in the correspondences. The thread ends with Aaron Whaley’s signature block reiterating his firm’s address and contact information.

item_237.note: Case: Greg-Neltner-MVA-4-1-2023. Client: Greg Neltner. Re: FW: PROGRESSIVE 23-6275504.

In late November 2023, Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm forwarded to Progressive an attached response to Whaley’s open records request regarding the Progressive files on Greg Neltner’s motor vehicle accident matter (Progressive 23-6275504). In his message, Whaley thanked Amy Morris for the update and stated that there is no body camera footage. He emphasized that the key information is the police report, which he said chronicles what Progressive’s insured told the officer at the scene and that this account is consistent with both Progressive’s insured’s statement and Mr. Neltner’s account. He noted that Progressive’s insured says she was rear-ended, and that the police report states the same. He also highlighted what the police report claims your insured said: that she crossed three lanes of traffic to get onto the northbound I-75 ramp and, as she did so, she turned in front of Mr. Neltner. Although the officer did not witness the incident and cannot testify to what happened, Whaley stated that the officer can testify about what Progressive’s insured said, and that the officer based his liability decision on that statement. Whaley further noted that in Greg Neltner’s recorded statement he said he did not see Progressive’s insured, a detail that aligns with the accident report’s language that Progressive’s insured “suddenly turned in front of him, leaving him no time to react.” Whaley added that the damage to Progressive’s insured vehicle is listed as “7 o’clock,” which he argued would be consistent with her claimed three-lane leftward crossing.

Amy Morris replied later that day with a message dated November 30, 2023. In that reply, she stated that the situation is a word-vs-word claim at this time. She explained that Progressive’s insured asserts she was rear-ended, while the statement from Mr. Neltner’s side says he did not know what happened and did not see their vehicle. Morris noted that the police report presents a third version. She indicated Progressive was seeking body camera footage to review what was actually said and viewed at the scene of the loss, and she stated that, given the information available, Progressive was advocating for their insured.

The email thread includes earlier communications as well. On October 17, 2023, Amy Morris sent to Aaron Whaley (and Justin Whaley) a message stating, “Please see the attached formal response to the demand for Gregory Neltner.” This was accompanied by the Progressive signature block and a note that the formal response had been attached.

Earlier, on June 28, 2023, Amy Morris had written to Aaron Whaley (and others) asking whether an email address could be provided for Jessa, in the context of the Progressive matter. The June 28, 2023 messages included the standard Progressive signatures and contact details.

On November 9, 2023, Amy Morris sent another note stating that she had received a voicemail but it was unclear who it was from, and that Progressive still stood by its liability decision and was waiting to obtain bodycam footage.

On November 29, 2023, 2:05 PM, Morris again referenced the Progressive 23-6275504 matter, noting that a response had previously been sent to Aaron on October 17. The content of that November 29 note reiterates the thread’s status and the prior October 17 document.

In sum, the correspondence reveals Progressive’s position that the police report contains crucial statements attributed to their insured, including the claim that she crossed three lanes to the NB I-75 ramp and turned in front of Mr. Neltner, with the police officer basing liability on that statement. Greg Neltner’s own recorded statement asserts he did not see Progressive’s insured, aligning with the report’s characterization that she suddenly turned in front of him. The damage description on the insured’s vehicle is noted as occurring at “7 o’clock,” which aligns with the insured’s three-lane-crossing narrative. Progressive has repeatedly requested bodycam footage to verify the scene’s statements and is advocating for their insured while maintaining its liability position, subject to the bodycam review.
